# Investigation: Stale Envoy Route Configuration After DestinationRule Update in Istio

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/istio--f8c9b973 (mirror of istio/istio)
**Task Type:** Deep Causal Chain (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

An Istio service mesh operator reports that updating a DestinationRule in their cluster **silently fails to propagate** to Envoy sidecars. Specifically, when they have multiple DestinationRules for the same host (e.g., one defining subsets, another defining traffic policy), updating one of them does not trigger an xDS push — the Envoy sidecar continues serving the **stale** cluster and route configuration.

The operator has two DestinationRules for `reviews.default.svc.cluster.local`:

**DR-1 (traffic policy):**
```yaml
apiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1alpha3
kind: DestinationRule
metadata:
  name: reviews-traffic-policy
  namespace: default
spec:
  host: reviews.default.svc.cluster.local
  trafficPolicy:
    connectionPool:
      tcp:
        maxConnections: 100
      http:
        h2UpgradePolicy: UPGRADE
```

**DR-2 (subsets):**
```yaml
apiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1alpha3
kind: DestinationRule
metadata:
  name: reviews-subsets
  namespace: default
spec:
  host: reviews.default.svc.cluster.local
  subsets:
    - name: v1
      labels:
        version: v1
    - name: v2
      labels:
        version: v2
```

When the operator updates `reviews-subsets` (e.g., adding a `v3` subset), the Envoy sidecar does **not** receive updated CDS/RDS config. Only restarting the pod picks up the change. Updating `reviews-traffic-policy` also has no effect.

Istio debug endpoint `GET /debug/config_dump` on the sidecar shows the old configuration even after the DestinationRule has been updated in the Kubernetes API server.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause of why updating a merged DestinationRule fails to trigger an xDS push, and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:

1. **How Istio merges multiple DestinationRules for the same host** — specifically the `mergeDestinationRule()` function in `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go` and how it combines subsets and traffic policies from multiple DRs into a single merged config
2. **How the merged DestinationRule loses identity metadata** — when two DRs are merged, only one DR's `config.Config` metadata (name/namespace) survives in the `consolidatedDestRules` structure. The metadata of contributing DRs is lost.
3. **How SidecarScope builds config dependencies** — the `AddConfigDependencies()` calls in `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go` that register which config resources a proxy depends on. Specifically, how `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` and `ConvertToSidecarScope()` iterate over `destinationRules` and add `ConfigKey{Kind: DestinationRule, Name: dr.Name, Namespace: dr.Namespace}` for each DR
4. **The specific gap: only one DR's ConfigKey is registered** — because the merged DR has only one name/namespace, `AddConfigDependencies` registers only that one DR. The other contributing DR(s) are not tracked.
5. **How the xDS push filter uses DependsOnConfig** — when a config change event occurs, `pilot/pkg/xds/` calls `SidecarScope.DependsOnConfig(configKey)` to decide if the proxy needs a push. If the updated DR is the one whose metadata was lost during merging, `DependsOnConfig` returns `false` and the push is **incorrectly skipped**.
6. **The relationship between PushContext.destinationRule() and the merge pipeline** — how `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go` stores the `destinationRuleIndex` and how `destinationRule()` returns the merged config, obscuring the fact that multiple DRs contributed to it

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Causal Chain
<Ordered list: symptom → intermediate hops → root cause>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy and diagnostic steps>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- The causal chain spans at least 4 packages: `pilot/pkg/model/`, `pilot/pkg/xds/`, `pilot/pkg/networking/core/`, and `pilot/pkg/config/`
- Focus on how the DestinationRule merging in `destination_rule.go` interacts with dependency tracking in `sidecar.go` and push filtering in the xDS layer

     1→# Investigation Report: Stale Envoy Route Configuration After DestinationRule Update
     2→
     3→## Summary
     4→
     5→When multiple DestinationRules target the same host, Istio merges them into a single consolidated configuration. However, only the metadata (Name/Namespace) of one DR survives this merge. When a proxy's SidecarScope registers config dependencies for the merged DR, it only registers the surviving DR's metadata, causing updates to the "absorbed" DRs to be silently skipped by xDS push filtering. The proxy continues serving stale configuration even though the DestinationRule has been updated in the Kubernetes API server.
     6→
     7→## Root Cause
     8→
     9→The root cause spans three interconnected systems:
    10→
    11→### 1. **DestinationRule Merging Loses Identity** (`pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go:38-109`)
    12→
    13→The `mergeDestinationRule()` function combines multiple DRs for the same host into a single merged entry:
    14→
    15→- **Line 41-42**: When a second DR for the same hostname exists, the code enters the merge path
    16→- **Line 65-66**: A deep copy of the existing DR is made: `copied := mdr.DeepCopy()` followed by `p.destRules[resolvedHost][i] = &copied`
    17→- **Lines 69-87**: Subsets from the new DR are appended to the merged rule
    18→- **Lines 91-93**: Traffic policy is merged (only if the existing rule doesn't have one)
    19→
    20→**The critical issue**: The metadata of the second DR (Name/Namespace from `destRuleConfig`) is **never persisted**. Only the first DR's `config.Config` object (with its original Name/Namespace) remains in `p.destRules[resolvedHost][i]`.
    21→
    22→When two DRs are present for the same host:
    23→- `reviews-traffic-policy` (v1, defining `TrafficPolicy`)
    2

The fix must restore the identity of all contributing DRs so that dependency tracking can account for them:

**Option 1: Track All Contributing DRs (Recommended)**
- Modify `consolidatedDestRules` struct to maintain a list of all contributing DR ConfigKeys for each merged entry
- Example: add field `contributingConfigs []model.ConfigKey` to track all DRs that were merged
- Update `mergeDestinationRule()` to populate this list
- Modify `AddConfigDependencies()` in SidecarScope to register all contributing DRs, not just the merged result
- This preserves the merged behavior while ensuring complete dependency tracking

**Option 2: Track Merged DR Configuration Separately**
- Maintain a separate index mapping from "merged DR" ConfigKey to "contributing DRs" ConfigKeys
- Intercept config change events to check both direct and contributing DR dependencies
- Less elegant but avoids modifying the merging logic

**Option 3: Disable Merging for Dependency Tracking**
- Keep the merged configuration for xDS generation (current behavior)
- But separately track each contributing DR's metadata for dependency purposes
- Update `SetDestinationRules()` to maintain a parallel map of all contributing DRs

   ```
   # Should show only one merged entry instead of two
   ```

61-assistanttext-
Excellent! I've completed a comprehensive investigation into the Istio DestinationRule merging issue. The report is now available at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

## Summary

The investigation reveals a **critical bug in dependency tracking** when multiple DestinationRules are merged for the same host:

### The Core Issue
When Istio merges multiple DestinationRules for the same host (e.g., one with traffic policy, one with subsets), it combines them into a single configuration object. However, **only one DR's metadata (Name/Namespace) survives the merge** - the other DR's identity is discarded. This causes the dependency tracking system to lose awareness of the absorbed DR, so updates to it are silently ignored by xDS push filtering.

### Causal Chain (7-step)
1. **Trigger**: Operator updates `reviews-subsets` DR
2. **First Hop**: Both DRs were already merged into one entry during initial load
3. **Second Hop**: SidecarScope only registers the surviving DR's metadata
4. **Third Hop**: Update event creates ConfigKey for `reviews-subsets`
5. **Root Cause**: The absorbed DR's ConfigKey was never tracked in dependencies
6. **Filter**: `DependsOnConfig()` returns false for the unregistered DR
7. **Result**: xDS push is skipped, proxy continues serving stale config

### Affected Code
- **Merging**: `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go:mergeDestinationRule()`
- **Storage**: `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:consolidatedDestRules`
- **Dependency Registration**: `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go:AddConfigDependencies()`
- **Push Filtering**: `pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go:ConfigAffectsProxy()`
- **Push Skip Decision**: `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go:688`

The report includes three recommended fix strategies and detailed diagnostic steps to confirm the issue in a live cluster.

Note that it does not perform inheritance style merging.\\n30: // IOW, given three dest rules (*.foo.com, *.foo.com, *.com), calling this function for\\n31: // each config will result in a final dest rule set (*.foo.com, and *.com).\\n32: //\\n33: // The following is the merge logic:\\n34: // 1. If the original rule did not have any top level traffic policy, traffic policies from the new rule will be\\n36: // used.\\n37: // 3. If the original rule did not have any exportTo, exportTo settings from the new rule will be used.\\n38: func (ps *PushContext) mergeDestinationRule(p *consolidatedDestRules, destRuleConfig mdr.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\\n46: \\t\\t\\tbothWithoutSelector := rule.GetWorkloadSelector() == nil && existingRule.GetWorkloadSelector() == nil\\n47: \\t\\t\\tbothWithSelector := existingRule.GetWorkloadSelector() != nil && rule.GetWorkloadSelector() != nil\\n48: \\t\\t\\tselectorsMatch := labels.Instance(existingRule.GetWorkloadSelector().GetMatchLabels()).Equals(rule.GetWorkloadSelector().GetMatchLabels())\\n49: \\n50: \\t\\t\\tif bothWithSelector && !selectorsMatch {\\n51: \\t\\t\\t\\t// If the new destination rule and the existing one has workload selectors associated with them, skip merging\\n52: \\t\\t\\t\\t// if the selectors do not match\\n53: \\t\\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n54: \\t\\t\\t}\\n55: \\n56: \\t\\t\\t// If both the destination rules are without a workload selector or with matching workload selectors, simply merge them.\\n57: \\t\\t\\t// If the incoming rule has a workload selector, it has to be merged with the existing rules with workload selector, and\\n58: \\t\\t\\t// at the same time added as a unique entry in the is a wrapper over the Sidecar resource with some\n56: // preprocessed data to determine the list of services, virtualServices,\n57: // and destinationRules that are accessible to a given\n58: // sidecar. Precomputing the list of services, virtual services, dest rules\n59: // for a sidecar improves performance as we no longer need to compute this\n60: // list for every sidecar. We simply have to match a sidecar to a\n61: // SidecarScope. Note that this is not the same as public/private scoped\n62: // services. The list of services seen by every sidecar scope (namespace\n63: // wide or per workload) depends on the imports, the listeners, and other\n64: // settings.\n65: //\n66: // Every proxy workload of SidecarProxy type will always map to a\n67: // SidecarScope object. If the proxy's namespace does not have a user\n68: // specified Sidecar CRD, we will construct one that has a catch all egress\n69: // listener that imports every public service/virtualService in the mesh.\n70: type SidecarScope struct {\n71: \tName string\n72: \t// This is the namespace where the sidecar takes effect,\n73: \t// maybe different from the ns where sidecar resides if sidecar is in root ns.\n74: \tNamespace string\n75: \t// The crd itself. Can be nil if we are constructing the default\n76: \t// sidecar scope\n77: \tSidecar *networking.Sidecar\n78: \n79: \t// Version this sidecar was computed for\n80: \tVersion string\n81: \n82: \t// Set of egress listeners, and their associated services.  A sidecar\n83: \t// scope should have either ingress/egress listeners or both.  For\n84: \t// every proxy workload that maps to a sidecar API object (or the\n85: \t// default object), we will go through every egress listener in the\n86: \t// object and process the Envoy listener or RDS based on the imported\n87: \t// services/virtual services in that listener.\n88: \tEgressListeners []*IstioEgressListenerWrapper\n89: \n90: \t// Union of services imported across all egress listeners for use by CDS code.\n91: \tservices           []*Service\n92: \tservicesByHostname map[host.Name]*Service\n93: \n94: \t// Destination rules imported across all egress listeners. This\n95: \t// contains the computed set based on public/private destination rules\n96: \t// as well as the inherited ones, in addition to the wildcard matches\n97: \t// such as *.com applying to foo.bar.com. Each hostname in this map\n98: \t// corresponds to a service in the services array above. When computing\n99: \t// CDS, we simply have to find the matching service and return the\n100: \t// destination rule.\n101: \tdestinationRules map[host.Name][]*config.Config\n102: \t// OutboundTrafficPolicy defines the outbound traffic policy for this sidecar.\n103: \t// If OutboundTrafficPolicy is ALLOW_ANY traffic to unknown destinations will\n104: \t// be forwarded.\n105: \tOutboundTrafficPolicy *networking.OutboundTrafficPolicy\n106: \n107: \t// Set of known configs this sidecar depends on.\n108: \t// This field will be used to determine the config/resource scope\n109: \t// which means which config changes will affect the proxies within this scope.\n110: \tconfigDependencies map[uint64]struct{}\n111: \n112: \t// The namespace to treat as the administrative root namespace for\n113: \t// Istio configuration.\n114: \t//\n115: \t// Changes to Sidecar resources in this namespace will trigger a push.\n116: \tRootNamespace string\n117: }\n118: \n119: // MarshalJSON implements json.Marshaller\n120: func (sc *SidecarScope) MarshalJSON() ([]byte, error) {\n121: \t// Json cannot expose unexported fields, so copy the ones we want here\n122: \treturn json.MarshalIndent(map[string]interface{}{\n123: \t\t\"version\":               sc.Version,\n124: \t\t\"rootNamespace\":         sc.RootNamespace,\n125: \t\t\"name\":                  sc.Name,\n126: \t\t\"namespace\":             sc.Namespace,\n127: \t\t\"outboundTrafficPolicy\": sc.OutboundTrafficPolicy,\n128: \t\t\"services\":              sc.services,\n129: \t\t\"sidecar\":               sc.Sidecar,\n130: \t\t\"destinationRules\":      sc.destinationRules,\n131: \t}, \"\", \"  \")\n132: }\n133: \n134: // IstioEgressListenerWrapper is a wrapper for\n135: // networking.IstioEgressListener object. The wrapper provides performance\n136: // optimizations as it allows us to precompute and store the list of\n137: // services/virtualServices that apply to this listener.\n138: type IstioEgressListenerWrapper struct {\n139: \t// The actual IstioEgressListener api object from the Config. It can be\n140: \t// nil if this is for the default sidecar scope.\n141: \tIstioListener *networking.IstioEgressListener\n142: \n143: \t// List of services imported by this egress listener above.\n144: \t// This will be used by LDS and RDS code when\n145: \t// building the set of virtual hosts or the tcp filterchain matches for\n146: \t// a given listener port. Two listeners, on user specified ports or\n147: \t// unix domain sockets could have completely different sets of\n148: \t// services. So a global list of services per sidecar scope will be\n149: \t// incorrect. Hence the per listener set of services.\n150: \tservices []*Service\n151: \n152: \t// List of virtual services imported by this egress listener above.\n153: \t// As with per listener services, this\n154: \t// will be used by RDS code to compute the virtual host configs for\n155: \t// http listeners, as well as by TCP/TLS filter code to compute the\n156: \t// service routing configs and the filter chain matches. We need a\n157: \t// virtualService set per listener and not one per sidecarScope because\n158: \t// each listener imports an independent set of virtual services.\n159: \t// Listener 1 could import a public virtual service for serviceA from\n160: \t// namespace A that has some path rewrite, while listener2 could import\n161: \t// a private virtual service for serviceA from the local namespace,\n162: \t// with a different path rewrite or no path rewrites.\n163: \tvirtualServices []config.Config\n164: \n165: \tlistenerHosts map[string][]host.Name\n166: }\n167: \n168: const defaultSidecar = \"default-sidecar\"\n169: \n170: // DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace is a sidecar scope object with a default catch all egress listener\n171: // that matches the default Istio behavior: a sidecar has listeners for all services in the mesh\n172: // We use this scope when the user has not set any sidecar Config for a given config namespace.\n173: func DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace(ps *PushContext, configNamespace string) *SidecarScope {\n174: \tdefaultEgressListener := &IstioEgressListenerWrapper{\n175: \t\tIstioListener: &networking.IstioEgressListener{\n176: \t\t\tHosts: []string{\"*/*\"},\n177: \t\t},\n178: \t}\n179: \tdefaultEgressListener.services = ps.servicesExportedToNamespace(configNamespace)\n180: \tdefaultEgressListener.virtualServices = ps.VirtualServicesForGateway(configNamespace, constants.IstioMeshGateway)\n181: \n182: \tout := &SidecarScope{\n183: \t\tName: defaultEgressListener.services,\n187: \t\tdestinationRules:   make(map[host.Name][]*config.Config),\n188: \t\tservicesByHostname: make(map[host.Name]*Service, \t}\n193: \n194: \t// Now that we have all the services that sidecars using this scope (in\n195: \t// this config namespace) will see, identify all the destinationRules\n196: \t// that these services need\n197: \tfor _, s := range out.services {\n198: \t\t// In some scenarios, there may be multiple Services defined for the same hostname due to ServiceEntry allowing\n199: \t\t// arbitrary In these cases, we want to pick the first Service, which is the oldest. This ensures\n200: \t\t// newly created Services cannot take ownership unexpectedly.\n201: \t\t// However, the Service is from Kubernetes it should take precedence over ones not. This prevents someone from\n202: \t\t// \"domain squatting\" on the hostname before a Kubernetes Service is created.\n203: \t\t// This relies on the assumption that\n204: \t\tif existing, f := \t\t}\n208: \t\tout.servicesByHostname[s.Hostname] = s\n209: \t\tif dr := ps.destinationRule(configNamespace, s); dr != nil {\n210: \t\t\tout.destinationRules[s.Hostname] = dr\n211: \t\t}\n212: \t\tout.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n213: \t\t\tKind:      gvk.ServiceEntry,\n214: \t\t\tName:      string(s.Hostname),\n215: \t\t\tNamespace: s.Attributes.Namespace,\n216: \t\t})\n217: \t}\n218: \n219: \tfor _, drList := range out.destinationRules {\n220: \t\tfor _, dr := range drList {\n221: \t\t\tout.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n222: \t\t\t\tKind:      gvk.DestinationRule,\n223: \t\t\t\tName:      dr.Name,\n224: \t\t\t\tNamespace: dr.Namespace,\n225: \t\t\t})\n226: \t\t}\n227: \t}\n228: \n229: \tfor _, el := range out.EgressListeners {\n230: \t\t// add dependencies on delegate virtual services\n231: \t\tdelegates := ps.DelegateVirtualServicesConfigKey(el.virtualServices)\n232: \t\tfor _, delegate := range delegates {\n233: \t\t\tout.AddConfigDependencies(delegate)\n234: \t\t}\n235: \t\tfor _, vs := range el.virtualServices {\n236: \t\t\tout.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n237: \t\t\t\tKind:      gvk.VirtualService,\n238: \t\t\t\tName:      vs.Name,\n239: \t\t\t\tNamespace: vs.Namespace,\n240: \t\t\t})\n241: \t\t}\n242: \t}\n243: \n244: \tif ps.Mesh.OutboundTrafficPolicy != nil {\n245: \t\tout.OutboundTrafficPolicy = &networking.OutboundTrafficPolicy{\n246: \t\t\tMode: networking.OutboundTrafficPolicy_Mode(ps.Mesh.OutboundTrafficPolicy.Mode),\n247: \t\t}\n248: \t}\n249: \n250: \treturn out\n251: }\n252: \n253: // ConvertToSidecarScope converts from Sidecar config to SidecarScope object\n254: func ConvertToSidecarScope(ps *PushContext, sidecarConfig *config.Config, configNamespace string) *SidecarScope {\n255: \tif sidecarConfig == nil {\n256: \t\treturn DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace(ps, configNamespace)\n257: \t}\n258: \n259: \tsidecar := \t// this sidecar crd. This is needed to generate CDS output\n288: \tout.services = make([]*Service, 0)\n289: \ttype serviceIndex struct {\n290: \t\tsvc   *Service\n291: \t\tindex int // index record the position of the svc in slice\n292: \t}\n293: \tservicesAdded := make(map[host.Name]serviceIndex)\n294: \taddService := func(s *Service) {\n295: \t\tif s == nil {\n296: \t\t\treturn\n297: \t\t}\n298: \t\tif foundSvc, else if foundSvc.svc.Attributes.Namespace == s.Attributes.Namespace && s.Ports != nil && len(s.Ports) > 0 {\n307: \t\t\t// merge the ports to service when each listener generates partial service\n308: \t\t\t// we only merge if the found service is in the same namespace as the one we're trying to add\n309: \t\t\tcopied := foundSvc.svc.DeepCopy()\n310: \t\t\tfor _, p := range s.Ports {\n311: \t\t\t\tfound := false\n312: \t\t\t\tfor _, osp := range copied.Ports {\n313: \t\t\t\t\tif p.Port == osp.Port {\n314: \t\t\t\t\t\tfound = true\n315: \t\t\t\t\t\tbreak\n316: \t\t\t\t\t}\n317: \t\t\t\t}\n318: \t\t\t\tif !found {\n319: \t\t\t\t\tcopied.Ports = append(copied.Ports, p)\n320: \t\t\t\t}\n321: \t\t\t}\n322: \t\t\t// replace service in slice\n323: needsPortMatch(listener)\n339: \t\t// Infer more possible destinations from virtual services\n340: \t\t// Services chosen here will not override services explicitly requested in listener.services.\n341: \t\t// That way, if there is ambiguity around what hostname to pick, a user can specify the one they\n342: \t\t// want in the hosts field, and the potentially random choice below won't matter\n343: \t\tfor _, vs := range listener.virtualServices {\n344: \t\t\tv := vs.Spec.(*networking.VirtualService)\n345: \t\t\tout.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n346: \t\t\t\tKind:      gvk.VirtualService,\n347: \t\t\t\tName:      vs.Name,\n348: \t\t\t\tNamespace: vs.Namespace,\n349: \t\t\t})\n350: \n351: \t\t\tfor _, h := range virtualServiceDestinationHosts(v) {\n352: \t\t\t\t// Default to this hostname in our config namespace\n353: \t\t\t\tif s, ok := ps.ServiceIndex.HostnameAndNamespace[host.Name(h)][configNamespace]; ok {\n354: \t\t\t\t\t// This won't overwrite hostnames that have already been found eg because they were requested in hosts\n355: \t\t\t\t\tvar vss *Service\n356: \t\t\t\t\tif matchPort {\n357: \t\t\t\t\t\tvss = serviceMatchingListenerPort(s, listener)\n358: \t\t\t\t\t} else {\n359: \t\t\t\t\t\tvss = s\n360: \t\t\t\t\t}\n361: \t\t\t\t\tif vss != nil {\n362: \t\t\t\t\t\taddService(vss)\n363: \t\t\t\t\t}\n364: \t\t\t\t} else {\n365: \n366: \t\t\t\t\t// We couldn't find the hostname in our config namespace\n367: \t\t\t\t\t// We have to pick one arbitrarily for now, so we'll pick the first namespace alphabetically\n368: \t\t\t\t\t// TODO: could we choose services more intelligently based on their ports?\n369: \t\t\t\t\tbyNamespace := ps.ServiceIndex.HostnameAndNamespace[host.Name(h)]\n370: \t\t\t\t\tif len(byNamespace) == 0 {\n371: \t\t\t\t\t\t// This hostname isn't found anywhere\n372: \t\t\t\t\t\tlog.Debugf(\"Could not find service hostname %s parsed from %s\", h, vs.Key())\n373: \t\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n374: \t\t\t\t\t}\n375: alphabetically\n385: \t\t\t\t\t\t// This won't overwrite hostnames that have already been found eg because they were requested in hosts\n386: \t\t\t\t\t\tvar vss *Service\n387: \t\t\t\t\t\tif services that sidecars using this scope (in\n402: \t// this config namespace) will see, identify all the destinationRules\n403: \t// that these services need\n404: \tout.servicesByHostname = make(map[host.Name]*Service, len(out.services))\n405: \tout.destinationRules = make(map[host.Name][]*config.Config)\n406: \tfor _, s := range out.services {\n407: \t\t\t\t})\n416: \t\t\t}\n417: \t\t}\n418: \t}\n419: \n420: \tif sidecar.OutboundTrafficPolicy == nil {\n421: \t\tif ps.Mesh.OutboundTrafficPolicy != nil {\n422: \t\t\tout.OutboundTrafficPolicy = &networking.OutboundTrafficPolicy{\n423: \t\t\t\tMode: networking.OutboundTrafficPolicy_Mode(ps.Mesh.OutboundTrafficPolicy.Mode),\n424: \t\t\t}\n425: \t\t}\n426: \t} else {\n427: \t\tout.OutboundTrafficPolicy = sidecar.OutboundTrafficPolicy\n428: \t}\n429: \n430: \treturn out\n431: }\n432: \n433: func convertIstioListenerToWrapper(ps *PushContext, configNamespace string,\n434: listener port or the bind address or the catch all listener\n465: func (sc *SidecarScope) GetEgressListenerForRDS(port int, bind string) *IstioEgressListenerWrapper {\n466: \tif sc == nil {\n467: \t\treturn nil\n468: \t}\n469: \n470: \tfor _, e := range sc.EgressListeners {\n471: \t\t// We hit a catchall listener. This is the last listener in the list of listeners\n472: \t\t// return as is\n473: \t\tif e.IstioListener == nil || e.IstioListener.Port == nil {\n474: \t\t\treturn e\n475: \t\t}\n476: \n477: \t\t// == 0 { // unix domain socket\n481: \t\t\t\tif e.IstioListener.Bind == bind {\n482: \t\t\t\t\treturn e\n483: \t\t\t\t}\n484: \t\t\t\t// no match.. continue searching\n485: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n486: \t\t\t}\n487: \t\t\t// this is a non-zero port match\n488: \t\t\treturn e\n489: \t\t}\n490: \t}\n491: \n492: \t// This should never be reached unless user explicitly set an empty array for egress\n493: \t// listeners which we actually forbid\n494: \treturn nil\n495: }\n496: \n497: // HasIngressListener returns if the sidecar scope has ingress listener set\n498: func (sc *SidecarScope) \treturn true\n508: }\n509: \n510: // Services returns the list of services imported by this egress listener\n511: func (ilw *IstioEgressListenerWrapper) Services() []*Service {\n512: \treturn ilw.services\n513: }\n514: \n515: // VirtualServices returns the list of virtual services imported by this\n516: // egress listener\n517: func (ilw *IstioEgressListenerWrapper) VirtualServices() []config.Config {\n518: \treturn ilw.virtualServices\n519: }\n520: \n521: // DependsOnConfig determines if the proxy depends on the given config.\n522: // Returns whether depends on this config or this kind of config is not scoped(unknown to be depended) here.\n523: func (sc *SidecarScope) DependsOnConfig(config ConfigKey) bool {\n524: \tif sc == nil {\n525: \t\treturn true\n526: \t}\n527: \n528: \t// This kind of config will trigger a change if made in the root namespace or the same namespace\n529: \tif _, f := clusterScopedConfigTypes[config.Kind]; f {\n530: \t\treturn sidecarScopeKnownConfigTypes[config.Kind]; !f {\n535: \t\treturn true\n536: \t}\n537: \n538: \t_, exists := sc.configDependencies[config.HashCode()]\n539: \treturn exists\n540: }\n541: \n542: // AddConfigDependencies add extra config dependencies to this scope. This action should be done before the\n543: // SidecarScope being used to avoid concurrent read/write.\n544: func (sc *SidecarScope) AddConfigDependencies(dependencies ...ConfigKey) {\n545: \tif sc == nil {\n546: \t\treturn\n547: \t}\n548: \tif sc.configDependencies == nil {\n549: \t\tsc.configDependencies = make(map[uint64]struct{})\n550: \t}\n551: \n552: \tfor _, config := range dependencies {\n553: \t\tsc.configDependencies[config.HashCode()] = struct{}{}\n554: \t}\n555: }\n556: \n557: // DestinationRule returns a destinationrule for a svc.\n558: func (sc *SidecarScope) {
  "content": "# Investigation Report: Stale Envoy Route Configuration After DestinationRule Update\n\n## Summary\n\nWhen multiple DestinationRules target the same host, Istio merges them into a single consolidated configuration. However, only the metadata (Name/Namespace) of one DR survives this merge. When a proxy's SidecarScope registers config dependencies for the merged DR, it only registers the surviving DR's metadata, causing updates to the \"absorbed\" DRs to be silently skipped by xDS push filtering. The proxy continues serving stale configuration even though the DestinationRule has been updated in the Kubernetes API server.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause spans three interconnected systems:\n\n### 1. **DestinationRule Merging Loses Identity** (`pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go:38-109`)\n\nThe `mergeDestinationRule()` function combines multiple DRs for the same host into a single merged entry:\n\n- **Line 41-42**: When a second DR for the same hostname exists, the code enters the merge path\n- **Line 65-66**: A deep copy of the existing DR is made: `copied := mdr.DeepCopy()` followed by `p.destRules[resolvedHost][i] = &copied`\n- **Lines 69-87**: Subsets from the new DR are appended to the merged rule\n- **Lines 91-93**: Traffic policy is merged (only if the existing rule doesn't have one)\n\n**The critical issue**: The metadata of the second DR (Name/Namespace from `destRuleConfig`) is **never persisted**. Only the first DR's `config.Config` object (with its original Name/Namespace) remains in `p.destRules[resolvedHost][i]`.\n\nWhen two DRs are present for the same host:\n- `reviews-traffic-policy` (v1, defining `TrafficPolicy`)\n- `reviews-subsets` (v2, defining `Subsets`)\n\nAfter merging, only `reviews-traffic-policy`'s metadata remains in the `consolidatedDestRules.destRules` map. The second DR's metadata is lost.\n\n### 2. **Dependency Tracking Only Registers Surviving Metadata** (`pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go:219-227, 410-415`)\n\nWhen a SidecarScope is created, it populates config dependencies:\n\n**In `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` (lines 219-227)**:\n```go\nfor _, drList := range out.destinationRules {\n    for _, dr := range drList {\n        out.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n            Kind:      gvk.DestinationRule,\n            Name:      dr.Name,              // Only ONE DR's metadata\n            Namespace: dr.Namespace,\n        })\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**In `ConvertToSidecarScope()` (lines 410-415)**:\n```go\nfor _, dr := range drList {\n    out.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n        Kind:      gvk.DestinationRule,\n        Name:      dr.Name,                 // Only ONE DR's metadata\n        Namespace: dr.Namespace,\n    })\n}\n```\n\nSince `drList` is populated from `ps.destinationRule(configNamespace, s)`, which queries the merged `destinationRuleIndex`, it only contains ONE `config.Config` object with only ONE set of metadata. The second DR's ConfigKey is never registered.\n\n**Result**: `configDependencies` contains only `{reviews-traffic-policy, default}` but NOT `{reviews-subsets, default}`.\n\n### 3. **xDS Push Filtering Skips Unregistered DRs** (`pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go:32-74`)\n\nWhen a DestinationRule is updated, the control plane creates a `PushRequest` with the updated DR's ConfigKey. The xDS discovery server uses `ConfigAffectsProxy()` to filter which proxies need an update:\n\n**Line 52-54 (`ConfigAffectsProxy`)**:\n```go\nif affected && checkProxyDependencies(proxy, config) {\n    return true\n}\n```\n\n**Lines 60-74 (`checkProxyDependencies`)**:\n```go\nfunc checkProxyDependencies(proxy *model.Proxy, config model.ConfigKey) bool {\n    switch proxy.Type {\n    case model.SidecarProxy:\n        if proxy.SidecarScope.DependsOnConfig(config) {\n            return true\n        } else if proxy.PrevSidecarScope != nil && proxy.PrevSidecarScope.DependsOnConfig(config) {\n            return true\n        }\n    ...\n    }\n    return false\n}\n```\n\n**Dependency Check (`sidecar.go:521-540`)**:\n```go\nfunc (sc *SidecarScope) DependsOnConfig(config ConfigKey) bool {\n    if sc == nil {\n        return true\n    }\n\n    // Check if this kind is cluster-scoped\n    if _, f := clusterScopedConfigTypes[config.Kind]; f {\n        return config.Namespace == sc.RootNamespace || config.Namespace == sc.Namespace\n    }\n\n    // Check if this kind is known\n    if _, f := sidecarScopeKnownConfigTypes[config.Kind]; !f {\n        return true\n    }\n\n    _, exists := sc.configDependencies[config.HashCode()]  // Line 538\n    return exists\n}\n```\n\nWhen `reviews-subsets` is updated:\n- A `PushRequest` with `ConfigKey{Kind: DestinationRule, Name: \"reviews-subsets\", Namespace: \"default\"}` is created\n- For each proxy, `DependsOnConfig()` is called with this key\n- Line 538 checks if this key's hashcode exists in `configDependencies`\n- Since only `reviews-traffic-policy`'s metadata was registered, this check fails\n- **`DependsOnConfig()` returns `false`**\n- `ConfigAffectsProxy()` returns `false`\n- The xDS push to this proxy is **skipped** (ads.go:688)\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References\n\n1. **DestinationRule Merging Loss of Metadata**\n   - File: `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go`\n   - Lines: 38-109, specifically lines 65-66 and 102\n   - The second DR's metadata is lost when merging into an existing entry\n\n2. **consolidatedDestRules Structure**\n   - File: `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`\n   - Lines: 251-256\n   - Structure stores only `destRules map[host.Name][]*config.Config`, losing track of contributing DRs\n\n3. **SidecarScope Dependency Registration**\n   - File: `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go`\n   - Lines: 219-227 (`DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace`)\n   - Lines: 410-415 (`ConvertToSidecarScope`)\n   - Only registers metadata for DRs visible in the merged `destinationRules` map\n\n4. **xDS Push Filtering**\n   - File: `pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go`\n   - Lines: 32-74 (`ConfigAffectsProxy`, `checkProxyDependencies`)\n   - File: `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go`\n   - Line: 688 - `if !s.ProxyNeedsPush(con.proxy, pushRequest)` skips the push\n\n5. **DependsOnConfig Check**\n   - File: `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go`\n   - Lines: 521-540\n   - Line 538 performs the hashcode lookup that fails for the absorbed DR\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go`**\n   - `mergeDestinationRule()` function\n   - Merges multiple DRs but loses identity of absorbed ones\n\n2. **`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`**\n   - `consolidatedDestRules` struct (lines 251-256)\n   - `destinationRuleIndex` struct (lines 111-119)\n   - `SetDestinationRules()` function (lines 1672-1744)\n   - `destinationRule()` function (lines 989-1066)\n   - Stores merged DRs without tracking all contributing DRs\n\n3. **`pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go`**\n   - `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` (lines 173-251)\n   - `ConvertToSidecarScope()` (lines 254-431)\n   - `DependsOnConfig()` (lines 521-540)\n   - `AddConfigDependencies()` (lines 542-555)\n   - Registers only visible DRs without accounting for absorbed ones\n\n4. **`pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go`**\n   - `ConfigAffectsProxy()` (lines 32-58)\n   - `checkProxyDependencies()` (lines 60-74)\n   - `DefaultProxyNeedsPush()` (lines 77-95)\n   - Filters pushes based on incomplete dependency information\n\n5. **`pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go`**\n   - Line 688-690: Push skip decision\n   - Uses `ProxyNeedsPush()` which internally calls `ConfigAffectsProxy()`\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Symptom**: Operator updates `reviews-subsets` DestinationRule \u2192 Envoy continues serving stale config \u2192 `/debug/config_dump` on sidecar shows old configuration\n\n2. **Trigger**: Update event occurs for `reviews-subsets` DR \u2192 control plane creates PushRequest with `ConfigKey{Kind: DestinationRule, Name: \"reviews-subsets\", Namespace: \"default\"}`\n\n3. **First Hop - Merge Already Happened**: During initial mesh configuration load, both `reviews-traffic-policy` and `reviews-subsets` DRs were processed by `SetDestinationRules()` (push_context.go:1672)\n   - Both target the same host: `reviews.default.svc.cluster.local`\n   - `mergeDestinationRule()` (destination_rule.go:38) merged them into one entry\n   - Only `reviews-traffic-policy`'s metadata survived in `consolidatedDestRules.destRules[hostname]`\n\n4. **Second Hop - Dependency Registration**: When the SidecarScope was created, `AddConfigDependencies()` was called for the merged DR list\n   - `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` or `ConvertToSidecarScope()` iterated over `destinationRules` map\n   - Since merging produced only one `config.Config` object (the surviving one), only `reviews-traffic-policy`'s ConfigKey was registered\n   - `reviews-subsets`'s ConfigKey was never added to `configDependencies`\n\n5. **Third Hop - Push Filter Check**: When the update event arrives for `reviews-subsets`, `ConfigAffectsProxy()` is called\n   - (proxy_dependencies.go:52): `checkProxyDependencies(proxy, {reviews-subsets, default})`\n   - (sidecar.go:538): `sc.DependsOnConfig()` checks if `{reviews-subsets, default}.HashCode()` exists in `configDependencies`\n   - The check fails because only `{reviews-traffic-policy, default}` was registered\n\n6. **Root Cause - Metadata Loss During Merge**: The fundamental issue is that `mergeDestinationRule()` (destination_rule.go:38-109) combines multiple DRs into a single `config.Config` object\n   - Line 66: `p.destRules[resolvedHost][i] = &copied` - only one DR's metadata persists\n   - The second DR's Name/Namespace are discarded\n   - `consolidatedDestRules.destRules` loses track of which DRs contributed to the merge\n\n7. **Final Result**: xDS push is skipped (ads.go:688) \u2192 proxy never receives update \u2192 Envoy continues using stale cluster and route configuration\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Root Cause Fix Strategy\n\nThe fix must restore the identity of all contributing DRs so that dependency tracking can account for them:\n\n**Option 1: Track All Contributing DRs (Recommended)**\n- Modify `consolidatedDestRules` struct to maintain a list of all contributing DR ConfigKeys for each merged entry\n- Example: add field `contributingConfigs []model.ConfigKey` to track all DRs that were merged\n- Update `mergeDestinationRule()` to populate sc.RootNamespace || config.Namespace == sc.Namespace\n    }\n\n    // Check if this kind is known\n    if _, f := sidecarScopeKnownConfigTypes[config.Kind]; !f {\n        return true\n    }\n\n    _, - Line 688-690: Push skip decision\n   - Uses `ProxyNeedsPush()` which internally calls `ConfigAffectsProxy()`\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Symptom**: Operator updates `reviews-subsets` DestinationRule \u2192 Envoy continues serving stale config \u2192 `/debug/config_dump` on sidecar shows old configuration\n\n2. **Trigger**: Update event occurs for `reviews-subsets` DR \u2192 control plane creates PushRequest with `ConfigKey{Kind: DestinationRule, Name: \"reviews-subsets\", Namespace: \"default\"}`\n\n3. **First Hop - Merge Already Happened**: During initial mesh configuration load, both `reviews-traffic-policy` and `reviews-subsets` DRs were processed by `SetDestinationRules()` (push_context.go:1672)\n   - Both target the same host: `reviews.default.svc.cluster.local`\n   - `mergeDestinationRule()` (destination_rule.go:38) merged them into one entry\n   - Only `reviews-traffic-policy`'s metadata survived in `consolidatedDestRules.destRules[hostname]`\n\n4. **Second Hop - Dependency Registration**: When the SidecarScope was created, `AddConfigDependencies()` was called for the merged DR list\n   - `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` or `ConvertToSidecarScope()` `mergeDestinationRule()` (destination_rule.go:38-109) combines multiple DRs into a single `config.Config` object\n   - Line 66: `p.destRules[resolvedHost][i] = &copied` - only one DR's metadata identity of all contributing DRs so that dependency tracking can account for them:\n\n**Option 1: Track All Contributing DRs (Recommended)**\n- Modify `consolidatedDestRules` struct to maintain a list of all contributing DR ConfigKeys for each merged entry\n- Example: add field `contributingConfigs []model.ConfigKey` to track all DRs that were merged\n- Update `mergeDestinationRule()` to populate this list\n- Modify `AddConfigDependencies()` in SidecarScope to register all contributing DRs, not just the merged result\n- This preserves the merged behavior while ensuring complete dependency tracking\n\n**Option 2: Track Merged DR Configuration Separately**\n- Maintain a separate index mapping from \"merged DR\" ConfigKey to \"contributing DRs\" ConfigKeys\n- Intercept config change events to check both direct and contributing DR dependencies\n- Less elegant but avoids modifying the merging logic\n\n**Option 3: Disable Merging for Dependency Tracking**\n- Keep the merged # Investigation Report: Stale Envoy Route Configuration After DestinationRule Update

## Summary

When multiple DestinationRules target the same host, Istio merges them into a single consolidated configuration. However, only the metadata (Name/Namespace) of one DR survives this merge. When a proxy's SidecarScope registers config dependencies for the merged DR, it only registers the surviving DR's metadata, causing updates to the "absorbed" DRs to be silently skipped by xDS push filtering. The proxy continues serving stale configuration even though the DestinationRule has been updated in the Kubernetes API server.

## Root Cause

The root cause spans three interconnected systems:

### 1. **DestinationRule Merging Loses Identity** (`pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go:38-109`)

The `mergeDestinationRule()` function combines multiple DRs for the same host into a single merged entry:

- **Line 41-42**: When a second DR for the same hostname exists, the code enters the merge path
- **Line 65-66**: A deep copy of the existing DR is made: `copied := mdr.DeepCopy()` followed by `p.destRules[resolvedHost][i] = &copied`
- **Lines 69-87**: Subsets from the new DR are appended to the merged rule
- **Lines 91-93**: Traffic policy is merged (only if the existing rule doesn't have one)

**The critical issue**: The metadata of the second DR (Name/Namespace from `destRuleConfig`) is **never persisted**. Only the first DR's `config.Config` object (with its original Name/Namespace) remains in `p.destRules[resolvedHost][i]`.

When two DRs are present for the same host:
- `reviews-traffic-policy` (v1, defining `TrafficPolicy`)
- `reviews-subsets` (v2, defining `Subsets`)

After merging, only `reviews-traffic-policy`'s metadata remains in the `consolidatedDestRules.destRules` map. The second
... (truncated)
